The <a href="/wiki/Financial_Innovation_and_Technology_for_the_21st_Century_Act" title="Financial Innovation and Technology for the 21st Century Act">Financial Innovation and Technology for the 21st Century Act</a>, which defines responsibilities between various US agencies, notably between the <a href="/wiki/Commodity_Futures_Trading_Commission" title="Commodity Futures Trading Commission">Commodity Futures Trading Commission</a> (CFTC) for decentralized blockchains and the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) for blockchains that are functional but not decentralized.  <a href="/wiki/Stablecoin" title="Stablecoin">Stablecoins</a> are excluded from both CFTC and SEC regulation in this bill, "except for fraud and certain activities by registered firms."<sup id="cite_ref-cfins20240510_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfins20240510-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="China">China</h3></div>
<p>In September 2017, China banned <a href="/wiki/Initial_coin_offering" title="Initial coin offering">ICOs</a> to cause <a href="/wiki/Abnormal_return" title="Abnormal return">abnormal return</a> from cryptocurrency decreasing during announcement window. The liquidity changes by banning ICOs in China was temporarily negative while the liquidity effect became positive after news.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 May 2021, China banned financial institutions and payment companies from being able to provide cryptocurrency transaction related services.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This led to a sharp fall in the price of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_work" title="Proof of work">proof of work</a> cryptocurrencies. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a> fell 31%, <a href="/wiki/Ethereum" title="Ethereum">Ethereum</a> fell 44%, <a href="/wiki/Binance#BNB" title="Binance">Binance Coin</a> fell 32% and <a href="/wiki/Dogecoin" title="Dogecoin">Dogecoin</a> fell 30%.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Proof of work mining was the next focus, with regulators in popular mining regions citing the use of electricity generated from highly polluting sources such as coal to create bitcoin and Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2021, the Chinese government declared all cryptocurrency transactions of any kind illegal, completing its crackdown on cryptocurrency.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cook_Islands">Cook Islands</h3></div>
<p>In April 2024, <a href="/wiki/TVNZ" title="TVNZ">TVNZ</a>'s <a href="/wiki/1News" title="1News">1News</a> reported that the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> government was proposing legislation that would allow "recovery agents" to use various means including hacking to investigate or find cryptocurrency that may have been used for illegal means or is the "proceeds of crime." The Tainted Cryptocurrency Recovery Bill was drafted by two lawyers hired by US-based debt collection company Drumcliffe. The proposed legislation was criticised by Cook Islands Crown Law's deputy solicitor general David Greig, who described it as "flawed" and said that some provisions were "clearly unconstitutional". The Cook Islands Financial Services Development Authority described Drumcliffe's involvement as a conflict of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-1_News_Cook_Islands_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1_News_Cook_Islands-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Similar criticism was echoed by <a href="/wiki/Auckland_University_of_Technology" title="Auckland University of Technology">Auckland University of Technology</a> cryptocurrency specialist and senior lecturer Jeff Nijsse and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Otago" title="University of Otago">University of Otago</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political scientist</a> Professor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Patman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Robert Patman (page does not exist)">Robert Patman</a>, who described it as government overreach and described it as inconsistent with international law. Since the Cook Islands is an <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated state</a> that is part of the <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">Realm of New Zealand</a>, Patman said that the law would have "implications for New Zealand's governance arrangements." A spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(New_Zealand)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (New Zealand)">New Zealand Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Peters" title="Winston Peters">Winston Peters</a> confirmed that New Zealand officials were discussing the legislation with their Cook Islands counterparts.  <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Cook_Islands" title="Prime Minister of the Cook Islands">Cook Islands Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Brown_(Cook_Islands)" title="Mark Brown (Cook Islands)">Mark Brown</a> defended the legislation as part of the territory's fight against international cybercrime.<sup id="cite_ref-1_News_Cook_Islands_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1_News_Cook_Islands-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="El_Salvador">El Salvador</h3></div>
<p>On 9 June 2021, <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> announced that it will adopt <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a> as legal tender, becoming the first country to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="EU">EU</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Markets_in_Crypto-Assets" title="Markets in Crypto-Assets">Markets in Crypto-Assets</a></div>
<p>The EU defines crypto assets as "a digital representation of a value or of a right that is able to be transferred and stored electronically using distributed ledger technology or similar technology."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The EU regulation Markets in Crypto-Assets (MiCA) covering asset-referenced tokens (ARTs) and electronic money tokens (EMTs) (also known as stablecoins) came into force on 30 June 2024. As of 17 January 2025, the <a href="/wiki/European_Securities_and_Markets_Authority" title="European Securities and Markets Authority">European Securities and Markets Authority</a> (ESMA) issued guidance to crypto-asset service providers (CASPs) allowing them to maintain crypto-asset services for non-compliant ARTs and EMTs until the end of March 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The rest of MiCA came into force as of 30 December 2024, covering crypto-assets other than ART and EMT and CASPs. MiCA excludes crypto-assets if they qualify as financial instruments according to ESMA guidelines published on 17 December 2024 as well as crypto-assets that are unique and not fungible with other crypto-assets.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="India">India</h3></div>
<p>At present, India neither prohibits nor allows investment in the cryptocurrency market. In 2020, the Supreme Court of India had lifted the ban on cryptocurrency, which was imposed by the Reserve Bank of India.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since then, an investment in cryptocurrency is considered legitimate, though there is still ambiguity about the issues regarding the extent and payment of tax on the income accrued thereupon and also its regulatory regime. But it is being contemplated that the Indian Parliament will soon pass a specific law to either ban or regulate the cryptocurrency market in India.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Expressing his public policy opinion on the Indian cryptocurrency market to a well-known online publication, a leading <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public policy</a> lawyer and Vice President of <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">SAARCLAW</a> (South Asian Association for Regional Co-operation in Law) <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hemant_Batra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hemant Batra (page does not exist)">Hemant Batra</a> has said that the "cryptocurrency market has now become very big with involvement of billions of dollars in the market hence, it is now unattainable and irreconcilable for the government to completely ban all sorts of cryptocurrency and its trading and investment".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He mooted regulating the cryptocurrency market rather than completely banning it. He favoured following <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force" title="Financial Action Task Force">FATF</a> guidelines in this regard.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Singapore">Singapore</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="South_Africa">South Africa</h3></div>
<p>South Africa, which has seen a large number of scams related to cryptocurrency, is said to be putting a regulatory timeline in place that will produce a regulatory framework.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest scam occurred in April 2021, where the two founders of an African-based cryptocurrency exchange called Africrypt, Raees Cajee and Ameer Cajee, disappeared with $3.8 billion worth of <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-regulations_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Mirror_Trading_International" title="Mirror Trading International">Mirror Trading International</a> disappeared with $170 million worth of cryptocurrency in January 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-regulations_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulations-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="South_Korea">South Korea</h3></div>
<p>In March 2021, South Korea implemented new legislation to strengthen their oversight of digital assets. This legislation requires all digital asset managers, providers and exchanges to be registered with the Korea Financial Intelligence Unit in order to operate in South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-thediplomat.com_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thediplomat.com-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Registering with this unit requires that all exchanges are certified by the Information Security Management System and that they ensure all customers have real name bank accounts. It also requires that the CEO and board members of the exchanges have not been convicted of any crimes and that the exchange holds sufficient levels of deposit insurance to cover losses arising from hacks.<sup id="cite_ref-thediplomat.com_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thediplomat.com-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Switzerland">Switzerland</h3></div>
<p>Switzerland was one of the first countries to implement the FATF's Travel Rule. FINMA, the Swiss regulator, issued its own guidance to VASPs in 2019. The guidance followed the FATF's Recommendation 16, however with stricter requirements. According to FINMA's<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> requirements, VASPs need to verify the identity of the beneficiary of the transfer.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Turkey">Turkey</h3></div>
<p>On 30 April 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey" title="Central Bank of the Republic of Turkey">Central Bank of the Republic of Turkey</a> banned the use of cryptocurrencies and <a href="/wiki/Cryptoassets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptoassets">cryptoassets</a> for making purchases on the grounds that the use of cryptocurrencies for such payments poses significant transaction risks.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_Arab_Emirates">United Arab Emirates</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</h3></div>
<p>In the United Kingdom, as of 10 January 2021, all cryptocurrency firms, such as exchanges, advisors and professionals that have either a presence, market product or provide services within the UK market must register with the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Conduct_Authority" title="Financial Conduct Authority">Financial Conduct Authority</a>. Additionally, on 27 June 2021, the financial watchdog demanded that <a href="/wiki/Binance" title="Binance">Binance</a>, the world's largest cryptocurrency exchange,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> cease all regulated activities in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ft.com_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft.com-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The incoming Labour government confirmed in November 2024 that it will proceed with the regulation of cryptoassets and new UK requirements are expected to come into force in 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_States">United States</h3></div>
<p>In 2021, 17 states in the US passed laws and resolutions concerning cryptocurrency regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This led the Securities and Exchange Commission to start considering what steps to take. On 8 July 2021, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Senator Elizabeth Warren</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Banking,_Housing,_and_Urban_Affairs" title="United States Senate Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs">Senate Banking Committee</a>, wrote to the chairman of the SEC and demanded answers on cryptocurrency regulation due to the increase in cryptocurrency exchange use and the danger this posed to consumers. On 5 August 2021, the chairman, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Gensler" title="Gary Gensler">Gary Gensler</a>, responded to Warren's letter and called for legislation focused on "crypto trading, lending and DeFi platforms," because of how vulnerable investors could be when they traded on crypto trading platforms without a broker. He also argued that many tokens in the crypto market may be unregistered securities without required disclosures or market oversight. Additionally, Gensler did not hold back in his criticism of stablecoins. These tokens, which are pegged to the value of fiat currencies, may allow individuals to bypass important public policy goals related to traditional banking and financial systems, such as anti-money laundering, tax compliance, and sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 October 2021, the first bitcoin-linked exchange-traded fund (ETF) from <a href="/wiki/ProShares" title="ProShares">ProShares</a> started trading on the NYSE under the ticker "BITO." <a href="/wiki/ProShares" title="ProShares">ProShares</a> CEO Michael L. Sapir said the ETF would expose bitcoin to a wider range of investors without the hassle of setting up accounts with cryptocurrency providers. Ian Balina, the CEO of Token Metrics, stated that SEC approval of the ETF was a significant endorsement for the crypto industry because many regulators globally were not in favor of crypto, and retail investors were hesitant to accept crypto. This event would eventually open more opportunities for new capital and new people in this space.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">Department of the Treasury</a>, on 20 May 2021, announced that it would require any transfer worth $10,000 or more to be reported to the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> since cryptocurrency already posed a problem where illegal activity like tax evasion was facilitated broadly. This release from the IRS was a part of efforts to promote better compliance and consider more severe penalties for tax evaders.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 February 2022, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Department of Justice</a> named Eun Young Choi as the first director of a National Cryptocurrency Enforcement Team to help identify and deal with misuse of cryptocurrencies and other digital assets.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Biden administration faced a dilemma as it tried to develop regulations for the cryptocurrency industry. On one hand, officials were hesitant to restrict a growing industry. On the other hand, they were committed to preventing illegal cryptocurrency transactions. To reconcile these conflicting goals, on 9 March 2022, Biden issued an executive order.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Followed this, on 16 September 2022, the Comprehensive Framework for Responsible Development of Digital Assets document was released<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to support development of cryptocurrencies and restrict their illegal use. The executive order included all digital assets, but cryptocurrencies posed both the greatest security risks and potential economic benefits. Though this might not address all of the challenges in crypto industry, it was a significant milestone in the US cryptocurrency regulation history.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2023, the SEC ruled that cryptocurrency exchange <a href="/wiki/Kraken_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraken (company)">Kraken</a>'s estimated $42 billion in staked assets globally operated as an illegal securities seller. The company agreed to a $30 million settlement with the SEC and to cease selling its staking service in the US. The case would impact other major crypto exchanges operating staking programs.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March 2023, the SEC issued an alert to investors stating that firms offering crypto asset securities might not be complying with US laws. The SEC argued that unregistered offerings of crypto asset securities might not include important information.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 January 2025, President Donald Trump signed <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_14178" title="Executive Order 14178">Executive Order 14178</a>, <i>Strengthening American Leadership in Digital Financial Technology</i><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> revoking <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_14067" title="Executive Order 14067">Executive Order 14067</a> of 9 March 2022, <i>Ensuring Responsible Development of Digital Assets</i> and the Department of the Treasury's <i>Framework for International Engagement on Digital Assets</i> of 7 July 2022.
In addition the order prohibits the establishment, issuance or promotion of <a href="/wiki/Central_bank_digital_currency" title="Central bank digital currency">Central bank digital currency</a> and establishes a group tasked with proposing a federal regulatory framework for digital assets within 180 days.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Legality">Legality</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">legal status of cryptocurrencies</a> varies substantially from country to country and is still undefined or changing in many of them. At least one study has shown that broad generalizations about the use of bitcoin in illicit finance are significantly overstated and that blockchain analysis is an effective crime fighting and intelligence gathering tool.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While some countries have explicitly allowed their use and trade,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> others have banned or restricted it. According to the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a>&#160;in 2021,
an "absolute ban" on trading or using cryptocurrencies applies in 9 countries:
Algeria, Bangladesh, Bolivia, China, Egypt, Iraq, Morocco, Nepal, and the United Arab Emirates. An "implicit ban" applies in another 39 countries or regions, which include: Bahrain, Benin, Burkina Faso, Burundi, Cameroon, Chad, Cote d’Ivoire, the Dominican Republic, Ecuador, Gabon, Georgia, Guyana, Indonesia, Iran, Jordan, Kazakhstan, Kuwait, Lebanon, Lesotho, Macau, Maldives, Mali, Moldova, Namibia, Niger, Nigeria, Oman, Pakistan, Palau, Republic of Congo, Saudi Arabia, Senegal, Tajikistan, Tanzania, Togo, Turkey, Turkmenistan, Qatar and Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWNov2021LOC_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWNov2021LOC-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the United States and Canada, state and provincial securities regulators, coordinated through the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Securities_Administrators_Association" title="North American Securities Administrators Association">North American Securities Administrators Association</a>, are investigating "Bitcoin scams" and <a href="/wiki/Initial_coin_offering" title="Initial coin offering">ICOs</a> in 40 jurisdictions.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo52118_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo52118-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Various government agencies, departments, and courts have classified bitcoin differently. <a href="/wiki/China_Central_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="China Central Bank">China Central Bank</a> banned the handling of bitcoins by financial institutions in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in early 2014.
</p><p>In Russia, though owning cryptocurrency is legal, its residents are only allowed to purchase goods from other residents using the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> while nonresidents are allowed to use foreign currency.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Regulations and bans that apply to bitcoin probably extend to similar cryptocurrency systems.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Thailand" title="Bank of Thailand">Bank of Thailand</a> announced its plans to create its own cryptocurrency, the Central Bank Digital Currency (CBDC).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Advertising_bans">Advertising bans</h3></div>
<p>Cryptocurrency advertisements have been banned on the following platforms:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a><sup id="cite_ref-ToISW_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToISW-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> - Ended August 2021<sup id="cite_ref-Search_Engine_Land_2021-06-03_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Search_Engine_Land_2021-06-03-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
