<li><a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a><sup id="cite_ref-bing51418_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bing51418-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> - Ended June 2022<sup id="cite_ref-Search_Engine_Land_2022-06-01_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Search_Engine_Land_2022-06-01-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Snapchat" title="Snapchat">Snapchat</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a><sup id="cite_ref-:3_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MailChimp" class="mw-redirect" title="MailChimp">MailChimp</a><sup id="cite_ref-3key_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3key-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tencent" title="Tencent">Tencent</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Weibo_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Weibo (company)">Weibo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_Corporation" title="Line Corporation">Line</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yandex" title="Yandex">Yandex</a><sup id="cite_ref-:3_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="U.S._tax_status">U.S. tax status</h3></div>
<p>On 25 March 2014, the United States <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> (IRS) ruled that bitcoin will be treated as property for tax purposes. Therefore, virtual currencies are considered commodities subject to capital gains tax.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Legal_concerns_relating_to_an_unregulated_global_economy">Legal concerns relating to an unregulated global economy</h3></div>
<p>As the popularity and demand for online currencies has increased since the inception of bitcoin in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> so have concerns that such an unregulated person to person global economy that cryptocurrencies offer may become a threat to society. Concerns abound that altcoins may become tools for anonymous web criminals.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Cryptocurrency networks display a lack of regulation that has been criticized as enabling criminals who seek to evade taxes and <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">launder money</a>. Money laundering issues <a href="/wiki/FinCEN_Files" title="FinCEN Files">are also present in regular bank transfers</a>, however with bank-to-bank wire transfers for instance, the account holder must at least <a href="/wiki/Wire_transfer#Security" title="Wire transfer">provide a proven identity</a>.
</p><p>Transactions that occur through the use and exchange of these altcoins are independent from formal banking systems, and therefore can make tax evasion simpler for individuals. Since charting taxable income is based upon what a recipient reports to the revenue service, it becomes extremely difficult to account for transactions made using existing cryptocurrencies, a mode of exchange that is complex and difficult to track.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Systems of anonymity that most cryptocurrencies offer can also serve as a simpler means to launder money. Rather than laundering money through an intricate net of financial actors and offshore bank accounts, laundering money through altcoins can be achieved through anonymous transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Cryptocurrency makes legal enforcement against extremist groups more complicated, which consequently strengthens them.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> White supremacist <a href="/wiki/Richard_B._Spencer" title="Richard B. Spencer">Richard Spencer</a> went as far as to declare bitcoin the "currency of the alt-right".<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Loss,_theft,_and_fraud"><span id="Loss.2C_theft.2C_and_fraud"></span>Loss, theft, and fraud</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_and_crime" title="Cryptocurrency and crime">Cryptocurrency and crime</a></div>
<p>In February 2014, the world's largest bitcoin exchange, <a href="/wiki/Mt._Gox" title="Mt. Gox">Mt. Gox</a>, declared <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a>. Likely due to theft, the company claimed that it had lost nearly 750,000 bitcoins belonging to their clients. This added up to approximately 7% of all bitcoins in existence, worth a total of $473 million. Mt. Gox blamed hackers, who had exploited the <a href="/wiki/Transaction_malleability_problem" title="Transaction malleability problem">transaction malleability problems</a> in the network. The price of a bitcoin fell from a high of about $1,160 in December to under $400 in February.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 November 2017, <a href="/wiki/Tether_(cryptocurrency)" title="Tether (cryptocurrency)">Tether</a> announced that it had been hacked, losing $31 million in USDT from its core treasury wallet.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 December 2017, Slovenian cryptocurrency exchange <a href="/wiki/NiceHash" title="NiceHash">Nicehash</a> reported that hackers had stolen over $70 million using a hijacked company computer.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 December 2017, Yapian, the owner of South Korean exchange Youbit, filed for bankruptcy after suffering two hacks that year.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Customers were still granted access to 75% of their assets.
</p><p>In May 2018, <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Gold" title="Bitcoin Gold">Bitcoin Gold</a> had its transactions hijacked and abused by unknown hackers.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Exchanges lost an estimated $18m and bitcoin Gold was delisted from Bittrex after it refused to pay its share of the damages.
</p><p>On 13 September 2018, Homero Josh Garza was sentenced to 21 months of imprisonment, followed by three years of supervised release.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Garza had founded the cryptocurrency startups GAW Miners and ZenMiner in 2014, acknowledged in a <a href="/wiki/Plea_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Plea agreement">plea agreement</a> that the companies were part of a <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_scheme" title="Pyramid scheme">pyramid scheme</a>, and pleaded guilty to <a href="/wiki/Wire_fraud" class="mw-redirect" title="Wire fraud">wire fraud</a> in 2015. The SEC separately brought a civil enforcement action in the US against Garza, who was eventually ordered to pay a judgment of $9.1 million plus $700,000 in interest. The SEC's complaint stated that Garza, through his companies, had fraudulently sold "investment contracts representing shares in the profits they claimed would be generated" from mining.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, Japanese exchange <a href="/wiki/Coincheck" title="Coincheck">Coincheck</a> reported that hackers had stolen cryptocurrency worth $530 million.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, South Korean exchange Coinrail was hacked, losing over $37 million in crypto.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hack worsened a cryptocurrency selloff by an additional $42 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 July 2018, the exchange Bancor, whose code and fundraising had been subjects of controversy, had $23.5 million in crypto stolen.<sup id="cite_ref-Bancorhack_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bancorhack-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A 2020 EU report found that users had lost crypto-assets worth hundreds of millions of US dollars in security breaches at exchanges and storage providers. Between 2011 and 2019, reported breaches ranged from four to twelve a year. In 2019, more than a billion dollars worth of cryptoassets was reported stolen. Stolen assets "typically find their way to illegal markets and are used to fund further criminal activity".<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2020 report produced by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">United States Attorney General</a>'s Cyber-Digital Task Force, three categories make up the majority of illicit cryptocurrency uses: "(1) financial transactions associated with the commission of crimes; (2) <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tax_evasion" title="Tax evasion">shielding of legitimate activity from tax</a>, reporting, or other legal requirements; or (3) crimes, such as theft, directly implicating the cryptocurrency marketplace itself." The report concluded that "for cryptocurrency to realize its truly transformative potential, it is imperative that these risks be addressed" and that "the government has legal and regulatory tools available at its disposal to confront the threats posed by cryptocurrency's illicit uses".<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to the UK 2020 national risk assessment—a comprehensive assessment of money laundering and terrorist financing risk in the UK—the risk of using cryptoassets such as bitcoin for money laundering and terrorism financing is assessed as "medium" (from "low" in the previous 2017 report).<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Legal scholars suggested that the money laundering opportunities may be more perceived than real.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_analysis" title="Blockchain analysis">Blockchain analysis</a> company Chainalysis concluded that illicit activities like <a href="/wiki/Cybercrime" title="Cybercrime">cybercrime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_financing" title="Terrorism financing">terrorism financing</a> made up only 0.15% of all crypto transactions conducted in 2021, representing a total of $14 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2021, Monkey Kingdom, a NFT project based in Hong Kong, lost US$1.3 million worth of cryptocurrencies via a phishing link used by the hacker.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 2, 2023, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Bankman-Fried" title="Sam Bankman-Fried">Sam Bankman-Fried</a> was pronounced guilty on seven counts of fraud related to <a href="/wiki/FTX" title="FTX">FTX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc-guilty_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-guilty-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Federal criminal court sentencing experts speculated on the potential amount of prison time likely to be meted out.<sup id="cite_ref-Livni_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Livni-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clifford_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clifford-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On March 28, 2024, the court sentenced Bankman-Fried to 25 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Money_laundering">Money laundering</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_and_crime" title="Cryptocurrency and crime">Cryptocurrency and crime</a></div>
<p>According to blockchain data company <a href="/wiki/Chainalysis" title="Chainalysis">Chainalysis</a>, criminals laundered <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>8,600,000,000 worth of cryptocurrency in 2021, up by 30% from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The data suggests that rather than managing numerous illicit havens, cybercriminals make use of a small group of purpose built centralized exchanges for sending and receiving illicit cryptocurrency. In 2021, those exchanges received 47% of funds sent by crime linked addresses.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Almost $2.2bn worth of cryptocurrencies was embezzled from DeFi protocols in 2021, which represents 72% of all cryptocurrency theft in 2021.
</p><p>According to <i>Bloomberg</i> and the <i>New York Times</i>, Federation Tower, a two skyscraper complex in the heart of Moscow City, is home to many cryptocurrency businesses under suspicion of facilitating extensive money laundering, including accepting illicit cryptocurrency funds obtained through scams, darknet markets, and ransomware.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Notable businesses include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Garantex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Garantex (page does not exist)">Garantex</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Eggchange, Cashbank, Buy-Bitcoin, Tetchange, Bitzlato, and Suex, which was sanctioned by the U.S. in 2021. Bitzlato founder and owner Anatoly Legkodymov was arrested following money-laundering charges by the United States Department of Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Dark money has also been flowing into Russia through a dark web marketplace called Hydra, which is powered by cryptocurrency, and enjoyed more than $1 billion in sales in 2020, according to Chainalysis.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The platform demands that sellers liquidate cryptocurrency only through certain regional exchanges, which has made it difficult for investigators to trace the money.
</p><p>Almost 74% of ransomware revenue in 2021 — over $400 million worth of cryptocurrency — went to software strains likely affiliated with Russia, where oversight is notoriously limited.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, Russians are also leaders in the benign adoption of cryptocurrencies, as the ruble is unreliable, and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">President Putin</a> favours the idea of "overcoming the excessive domination of the limited number of reserve currencies."<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, RenBridge - an unregulated alternative to exchanges for transferring value between blockchains - was found to be responsible for the laundering of at least $540 million since 2020. It is especially popular with people attempting to launder money from theft. This includes a cyberattack on Japanese crypto exchange Liquid that has been linked to <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Darknet_markets">Darknet markets</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Darknet_market" title="Darknet market">Darknet market</a></div>
<p>Properties of cryptocurrencies gave them popularity in applications such as a safe haven in banking crises and means of payment, which also led to the cryptocurrency use in controversial settings in the form of <a href="/wiki/Darknet_market" title="Darknet market">online black markets</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road_(marketplace)" title="Silk Road (marketplace)">Silk Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_190-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The original Silk Road was shut down in October 2013 and there have been two more versions in use since then. In the year following the initial shutdown of Silk Road, the number of prominent dark markets increased from four to twelve, while the amount of drug listings increased from 18,000 to 32,000.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_190-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Darknet markets present challenges in regard to legality. Cryptocurrency used in dark markets are not clearly or legally classified in almost all parts of the world. In the US, bitcoins are regarded as "virtual assets".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This type of ambiguous classification puts pressure on law enforcement agencies around the world to adapt to the shifting drug trade of dark markets.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (November 2019)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Wash_trades">Wash trades</h3></div>
<p>Various studies have found that crypto-trading is rife with <a href="/wiki/Wash_trade" title="Wash trade">wash trading</a>. Wash trading is a process, illegal in some jurisdictions, involving buyers and sellers being the same person or group, and may be used to manipulate the price of a cryptocurrency or inflate volume artificially. Exchanges with higher volumes can demand higher premiums from token issuers.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A study from 2019 concluded that up to 80% of trades on unregulated cryptocurrency exchanges could be wash trades.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2019 report by Bitwise Asset Management claimed that 95% of all bitcoin trading volume reported on major website CoinMarketCap had been artificially generated, and of 81 exchanges studied, only 10 provided legitimate volume figures.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="As_a_tool_to_evade_sanctions">As a tool to evade sanctions</h3></div>
<p>In 2022, cryptocurrencies attracted attention when Western nations imposed severe economic sanctions on Russia in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">its invasion of Ukraine</a> in February. However, American sources warned in March that some crypto-transactions could potentially be used to evade economic sanctions against Russia and Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, the computer programmer <a href="/wiki/Virgil_Griffith" title="Virgil Griffith">Virgil Griffith</a> received a five-year prison sentence in the US for attending a Pyongyang cryptocurrency conference, where he gave a presentation on blockchains which might be used for sanctions evasion.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Impacts_and_analysis">Impacts and analysis</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1257001546">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data:not(.notheme)>div:not(.notheme)[style]{background:#1f1f23!important;color:#f8f9fa}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data:not(.notheme) div:not(.notheme){background:#1f1f23!important;color:#f8f9fa}}@media(min-width:640px){body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table{display:table!important}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table>caption{display:table-caption!important}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table>tbody{display:table-row-group}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table tr{display:table-row!important}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table th,body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output .infobox-table td{padding-left:inherit;padding-right:inherit}}</style><table class="infobox" style="width: 210px; clear: right; float:right;margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="font-size:115%">External videos</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="text-align: left"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="video icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></span></span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vo6s1mUjxQQ">Cryptocurrencies: looking beyond the hype</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyun_Song_Shin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyun Song Shin">Hyun Song Shin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_for_International_Settlements" title="Bank for International Settlements">Bank for International Settlements</a>, 2:48<sup id="cite_ref-bis_report_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bis_report-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_for_International_Settlements" title="Bank for International Settlements">Bank for International Settlements</a> summarized several criticisms of cryptocurrencies in Chapter V of their 2018 annual report. The criticisms include the lack of stability in their price, the high energy consumption, high and variable transactions costs, the poor security and fraud at cryptocurrency exchanges, vulnerability to debasement (from forking), and the influence of miners.<sup id="cite_ref-bis_report_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bis_report-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chapterV_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapterV-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LATHiltzik_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATHiltzik-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Speculation,_fraud,_and_adoption"><span id="Speculation.2C_fraud.2C_and_adoption"></span>Speculation, fraud, and adoption</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_bubble" title="Cryptocurrency bubble">Cryptocurrency bubble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_and_crime" title="Cryptocurrency and crime">Cryptocurrency and crime</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_network" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitcoin network">Criminal activity on Bitcoin's network</a></div>
<p>Cryptocurrencies have been compared to <a href="/wiki/Ponzi_schemes" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponzi schemes">Ponzi schemes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_scheme" title="Pyramid scheme">pyramid schemes</a><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_bubble" title="Economic bubble">economic bubbles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Housing_market_bubble" class="mw-redirect" title="Housing market bubble">housing market bubbles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Marks_(investor)" title="Howard Marks (investor)">Howard Marks</a> of <a href="/wiki/Oaktree_Capital_Management" title="Oaktree Capital Management">Oaktree Capital Management</a> stated in 2017 that digital currencies were "nothing but an unfounded fad (or perhaps even a pyramid scheme), based on a willingness to ascribe value to something that has little or none beyond what people will pay for it", and compared them to the <a href="/wiki/Tulip_mania" title="Tulip mania">tulip mania</a> (1637), <a href="/wiki/South_Sea_Bubble" class="mw-redirect" title="South Sea Bubble">South Sea Bubble</a> (1720), and <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a> (1999), which all experienced profound price booms and busts.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Regulators in several countries have warned against cryptocurrency and some have taken measures to dissuade users.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, research in 2021 by the UK's financial regulator suggests such warnings either went unheard, or were ignored. Fewer than one in 10 potential cryptocurrency buyers were aware of consumer warnings on the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Conduct_Authority" title="Financial Conduct Authority">FCA</a> website, and 12% of crypto users were not aware that their holdings were not protected by <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Compensation_Scheme" title="Financial Services Compensation Scheme">statutory compensation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Of 1,000 respondents between the ages of eighteen and forty, almost 70% wrongly assumed cryptocurrencies were regulated, 75% of younger crypto investors claimed to be driven by competition with friends and family, 58% said that social media enticed them to make high risk investments.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The FCA recommends making use of its warning list, which flags unauthorized financial firms.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many banks do not offer virtual currency services themselves and can refuse to do business with virtual currency companies.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2014, Gareth Murphy, a senior banking officer, suggested that the widespread adoption of cryptocurrencies may lead to too much money being <a href="/wiki/Obfuscation" title="Obfuscation">obfuscated</a>, blinding economists who would use such information to better steer the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While traditional financial products have strong consumer protections in place, there is no intermediary with the power to limit consumer losses if bitcoins are lost or stolen. One of the features cryptocurrency lacks in comparison to credit cards, for example, is consumer protection against fraud, such as <a href="/wiki/Chargeback" title="Chargeback">chargebacks</a>.
</p><p>The French regulator <a href="/wiki/Autorit%C3%A9_des_march%C3%A9s_financiers_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autorité des marchés financiers (France)">Autorité des marchés financiers</a> (AMF) lists 16 websites of companies that solicit investment in cryptocurrency without being authorized to do so in France.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An October 2021 paper by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Economic_Research" title="National Bureau of Economic Research">National Bureau of Economic Research</a> found that bitcoin suffers from systemic risk as the top 10,000 addresses control about one-third of all bitcoin in circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is even worse for miners, with 0.01% controlling 50% of the capacity. According to researcher Flipside Crypto, less than 2% of anonymous accounts control 95% of all available bitcoin supply.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is considered risky as a great deal of the market is in the hands of a few entities.
</p><p>A paper by John Griffin, a finance professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas</a>, and Amin Shams, a graduate student found that in 2017 the price of bitcoin had been substantially inflated using another cryptocurrency, Tether.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Lowenstein" title="Roger Lowenstein">Roger Lowenstein</a>, author of "<i>Bank of America: The Epic Struggle to Create the Federal Reserve,</i>" says in a New York Times story that FTX will face over $8 billion in claims.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Non-fungible_tokens">Non-fungible tokens</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">Non-fungible tokens</a> (NFTs) are digital assets that represent art, collectibles, gaming, etc. Like crypto, their data is stored on the blockchain. NFTs are bought and traded using cryptocurrency. The Ethereum blockchain was the first place where NFTs were implemented, but now many other blockchains have created their own versions of NFTs.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Banks">Banks</h3></div>
<p>According to Vanessa Grellet, renowned panelist in blockchain conferences,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> there was an increasing interest from traditional <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchanges</a> in crypto-assets at the end of the 2010s, while crypto-exchanges such as <a href="/wiki/Coinbase" title="Coinbase">Coinbase</a> were gradually entering the traditional <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>. This convergence marked a significant trend where conventional financial actors were adopting blockchain technology to enhance operational efficiency, while the crypto world introduced innovations like <a href="/wiki/Security_token_offering" title="Security token offering">Security Token Offering</a> (STO), enabling new ways of <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">fundraising</a>. Tokenization, turning assets such as <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Investment_fund" title="Investment fund">investment funds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> into blockchain-based tokens, had the potential to make traditionally illiquid assets more accessible to investors. Despite the regulatory risks associated with such developments, major financial institutions, including <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, were actively working on blockchain initiatives, exemplified by the creation of Quorum, a private blockchain platform.<sup id="cite_ref-LT_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LT-252"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As the first big Wall Street bank to embrace cryptocurrencies, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a> announced on 17 March 2021 that they will be offering access to bitcoin funds for their wealthy clients through three funds which enable bitcoin ownership for investors with an aggressive risk tolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> BNY Mellon on 11 February 2021 announced that it would begin offering cryptocurrency services to its clients.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April 2021,<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Venmo" title="Venmo">Venmo</a> added support to its platform to enable customers to buy, hold and sell cryptocurrencies.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2021, financial services company <a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard">Mastercard</a> announced it is working with digital asset manager <a href="/wiki/Bakkt" title="Bakkt">Bakkt</a> on a platform that would allow any bank or merchant on the Mastercard network to offer cryptocurrency services.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_effects_of_bitcoin" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental effects of bitcoin">Environmental effects of bitcoin</a></div>
<p>Mining for <a href="/wiki/Proof-of-work" class="mw-redirect" title="Proof-of-work">proof-of-work</a> cryptocurrencies requires enormous amounts of electricity and consequently comes with a large <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> due to causing <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Proof-of-work blockchains such as bitcoin, <a href="/wiki/Ethereum" title="Ethereum">Ethereum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Litecoin" title="Litecoin">Litecoin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monero" title="Monero">Monero</a> were estimated to have added between 3 million and 15 million tons of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth&#39;s atmosphere">carbon dioxide (CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>) to the atmosphere</a> in the period from 1 January 2016 to 30 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By November 2018, bitcoin was estimated to have an annual <a href="/wiki/Energy_consumption" title="Energy consumption">energy consumption</a> of 45.8TWh, generating 22.0 to 22.9 million tons of CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>, rivalling nations like <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the end of 2021, bitcoin was estimated to produce 65.4 million tons of CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>, as much as <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and consume between 91 and 177 terawatt-hours annually.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Critics have also identified a large <a href="/wiki/Electronic_waste" title="Electronic waste">electronic waste</a> problem in disposing of <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_mining" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitcoin mining">mining rigs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mining hardware is improving at a fast rate, quickly resulting in older generations of hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bitcoin is the least energy-efficient cryptocurrency, using 707.6 kilowatt-hours of electricity per transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Before June 2021, China was the primary location for bitcoin mining. However, due to concerns over power usage and other factors, China forced out bitcoin operations, at least temporarily. As a result, the United States promptly emerged as the top global leader in the industry. An example of a gross amount of electronic waste associated with bitcoin mining operations in the US is a facility that located in Dalton, Georgia which is consuming nearly the same amount of electricity as the combined power usage of 97,000 households in its vicinity. Another example is that Riot Platforms operates a bitcoin mining facility in Rockdale, Texas, which consumes approximately as much electricity as the nearby 300,000 households. This makes it the most energy-intensive bitcoin mining operation in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The world's second-largest cryptocurrency, Ethereum, uses 62.56 kilowatt-hours of electricity per transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/XRP" class="mw-redirect" title="XRP">XRP</a> is the world's most energy efficient cryptocurrency, using 0.0079 kilowatt-hours of electricity per transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-laptopmag_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laptopmag-269"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>269<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although the biggest PoW blockchains consume energy on the scale of medium-sized countries, the annual power demand from proof-of-stake (PoS) blockchains is on a scale equivalent to a housing estate. <i>The Times</i> identified six "environmentally friendly" cryptocurrencies: <a href="/wiki/Chia_(cryptocurrency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chia (cryptocurrency)">Chia</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOTA_(technology)" title="IOTA (technology)">IOTA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardano_(blockchain_platform)" title="Cardano (blockchain platform)">Cardano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nano_(cryptocurrency)" title="Nano (cryptocurrency)">Nano</a>, Solarcoin and Bitgreen.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>270<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Academics and researchers have used various methods for estimating the energy use and energy efficiency of blockchains. A study of the six largest proof-of-stake networks in May 2021 concluded:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cardano_(blockchain_platform)" title="Cardano (blockchain platform)">Cardano</a> has the lowest electricity use per node;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Polkadot_(cryptocurrency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polkadot (cryptocurrency)">Polkadot</a> has the lowest electricity use overall; and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Solana_(blockchain_platform)" title="Solana (blockchain platform)">Solana</a> has the lowest electricity use per transaction.</li></ul>
<p>In terms of annual consumption (kWh/yr), the figures were: Polkadot (70,237), <a href="/wiki/Tezos" title="Tezos">Tezos</a> (113,249), <a href="/wiki/Avalanche_(blockchain_platform)" title="Avalanche (blockchain platform)">Avalanche</a> (489,311), <a href="/wiki/Algorand" title="Algorand">Algorand</a> (512,671), Cardano (598,755) and Solana (1,967,930). This equates to Polkadot consuming 7 times the electricity of an average U.S. home, Cardano 57 homes and Solana 200 times as much. The research concluded that PoS networks consumed 0.001% the electricity of the bitcoin network.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>271<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> University College London researchers reached a similar conclusion.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>272<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">Variable renewable energy</a> power stations could invest in bitcoin mining to reduce <a href="/wiki/Curtailment_(electricity)" title="Curtailment (electricity)">curtailment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedge_(finance)" title="Hedge (finance)">hedge</a> <a href="/wiki/Electricity_market#Risk_management" title="Electricity market">electricity price risk</a>, stabilize the grid, increase the <a href="/wiki/Energy_return_on_investment" title="Energy return on investment">profitability of renewable energy</a> power stations and therefore accelerate <a href="/wiki/Transition_to_sustainable_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Transition to sustainable energy">transition to sustainable energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fridgen2021_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fridgen2021-273"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>273<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>277<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Technological_limitations">Technological limitations</h3></div>
<p>There are also purely technical elements to consider. For example, technological advancement in cryptocurrencies such as bitcoin result in high up-front costs to miners in the form of specialized <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">hardware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>278<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cryptocurrency transactions are normally irreversible after a number of blocks confirm the transaction. Additionally, cryptocurrency private keys can be permanently lost from local storage due to malware, data loss or the destruction of the physical media. This precludes the cryptocurrency from being spent, resulting in its effective removal from the markets.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>279<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Academic_studies">Academic studies</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ledger_(journal)" title="Ledger (journal)">Ledger (journal)</a></div>
<p>In September 2015, the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Peer-reviewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-reviewed">peer-reviewed</a> <a href="/wiki/Academic_journal" title="Academic journal">academic journal</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Ledger_(journal)" title="Ledger (journal)">Ledger</a></i> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238218222">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit;word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}@media screen{.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}</style><a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/search?fq=x0:jrnl&amp;q=n2:2379-5980">2379-5980</a>) was announced. It covers studies of cryptocurrencies and related technologies, and is published by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>280<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The journal encourages authors to <a href="/wiki/Digital_signature" title="Digital signature">digitally sign</a> a <a href="/wiki/Hash_function" title="Hash function">file hash</a> of submitted papers, which will then be <a href="/wiki/Trusted_timestamping" title="Trusted timestamping">timestamped</a> into the bitcoin <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_(database)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockchain (database)">blockchain</a>. Authors are also asked to include a personal bitcoin address in the first page of their papers.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>281<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>282<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Aid_agencies">Aid agencies</h3></div>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Aid_agency" title="Aid agency">aid agencies</a> have started accepting donations in cryptocurrencies, including <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ibtimesunicef_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimesunicef-283"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>283<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Christopher Fabian, principal adviser at UNICEF Innovation, said the children's fund would uphold donor protocols, meaning that people making donations online would have to pass checks before they were allowed to deposit funds.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>However, in 2021, there was a backlash against donations in bitcoin because of the environmental emissions it caused. Some agencies stopped accepting bitcoin and others turned to "greener" cryptocurrencies.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>286<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace_USA" title="Greenpeace USA">U.S. arm of Greenpeace</a> stopped accepting bitcoin donations after seven years. It said: "As the amount of energy needed to run bitcoin became clearer, this policy became no longer tenable."<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>287<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian government">Ukrainian government</a> raised over <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>10,000,000 worth of aid through cryptocurrency following the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>288<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Criticism">Criticism</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">Bitcoin</a> has been characterized as a <a href="/wiki/Speculative_bubble" class="mw-redirect" title="Speculative bubble">speculative bubble</a> by eight <a href="/wiki/Winners_of_the_Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Winners of the Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">winners of the Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a>: <a href="/wiki/Paul_Krugman" title="Paul Krugman">Paul Krugman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_J._Shiller" title="Robert J. Shiller">Robert J. Shiller</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Shiller_2014_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shiller_2014-290"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>290<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stiglitz" title="Joseph Stiglitz">Joseph Stiglitz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Stiglitz_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stiglitz-291"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>291<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Thaler" title="Richard Thaler">Richard Thaler</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Thaler_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thaler-292"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>292<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Heckman" title="James Heckman">James Heckman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4Nobels_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Nobels-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sargent" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Sargent">Thomas Sargent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4Nobels_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Nobels-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Angus_Deaton" title="Angus Deaton">Angus Deaton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4Nobels_293-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Nobels-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hart_(economist)" title="Oliver Hart (economist)">Oliver Hart</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-4Nobels_293-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Nobels-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and by central bank officials including <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kearns_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kearns-294"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Carstens" title="Agustín Carstens">Agustín Carstens</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Carstens_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carstens-295"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADtor_Const%C3%A2ncio" title="Vítor Constâncio">Vítor Constâncio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Constancio_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constancio-296"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>296<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nout_Wellink" title="Nout Wellink">Nout Wellink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tulip_mania_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tulip_mania-297"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>297<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Investors <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Soros" title="George Soros">George Soros</a> have respectively characterized it as a "mirage"<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>298<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a "bubble";<sup id="cite_ref-GnMSoros_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GnMSoros-299"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>299<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while business executives <a href="/wiki/Jack_Ma" title="Jack Ma">Jack Ma</a> and <a href="/wiki/JP_Morgan_Chase" class="mw-redirect" title="JP Morgan Chase">JP Morgan Chase</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a> have called it a "bubble"<sup id="cite_ref-Yang_Ma_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_Ma-300"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>300<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a "fraud",<sup id="cite_ref-Buffet_and_Dimon_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buffet_and_Dimon-301"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>301<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> respectively, although Jamie Dimon later said he regretted dubbing bitcoin a fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>302<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Laurence_D._Fink" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurence D. Fink">Laurence D. Fink</a> called bitcoin an "index of <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>303<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, business magnate <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> said that cryptocurrencies are "100% based on <a href="/wiki/Greater_fool_theory" title="Greater fool theory">greater fool theory</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>304<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Legal scholars criticize the lack of regulation, which hinders conflict resolution when crypto assets are at the center of a legal dispute, for example a divorce or an inheritance. In Switzerland, jurists generally deny that cryptocurrencies are objects that fall under <a href="/wiki/Property_law" title="Property law">property law</a>, as cryptocurrencies do not belong to any class of legally defined objects (<i>Typenzwang</i>, the legal <a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus_(law)" title="Numerus clausus (law)">numerus clausus</a>). Therefore, it is debated whether anybody could even be sued for <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzlement</a> of cryptocurrency if he/she had access to someone's wallet. However, in the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_obligations" title="Law of obligations">law of obligations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contract law</a>, any kind of object would be legally valid, but the object would have to be tied to an identified <a href="/wiki/Counterparty" title="Counterparty">counterparty</a>. However, as the more popular cryptocurrencies can be freely and quickly exchanged into legal tender, they are financial assets and have to be taxed and accounted for as such.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>305<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>306<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, an increase in crypto-related suicides was noticed after the cryptocurrency market crashed in August. The situation was particularly critical in Korea as crypto traders were on "suicide watch". A cryptocurrency forum on Reddit even started providing suicide prevention support to affected investors.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>307<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>308<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The May 2022 collapse of the Luna currency operated by <a href="/wiki/Terra_(blockchain)" title="Terra (blockchain)">Terra</a> also led to reports of suicidal investors in crypto-related subreddits.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>309<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
